31

There's a long story involving the guestbook. Angela and Chris neglected to find one, but Kim, the wedding planner, had it in hand, or so she thought. When she got to the reception the bartenders had set up over the table under which she'd placed it, and she couldn't find it. She tried bribing Aaron to crawl under the tables looking for it but he couldn't find it either. Finally one of the bartenders found it while looking for something else.

Rob plays with his new zoom


As Canon afficionados will recognize, it's a 100-400/4.5-5.6L with image stabilization, Canon's best zoom in the 200-400 range (until they release the rumored 200-400/4 DO) and probably a better choice for shooting soccer with a film camera than my 70-200/2.8L IS and 1.4x teleconverter.  The rest of you can just say "that's a big lens".

Another pepper pitcher

There was some confusion about the rules for pitchers...the Pepper coach thought the usual seven inning per week limit held, and switched pitchers to save their best one for later, while we played our best pitcher (Breanna) the whole game with the understanding that (to avoid giving teams with byes an unfair advantage) the first round of playoffs counted as a separate week.

##-----------------TITLE------------------------##
Bottle figures
##------------------TEXT------------------------##
Prev: Through the windowUp: Museu d'Art ContemporaniNext: Lit bottles
Bottle figures

This was my favorite exhibit in the museum.  An inscription on the entrance said something about how, in the older days when women would wash the floors on their knees every day, it made a gesture very similar to prayer.  In this dark room, projectors cast shadows of cleaning liquid bottles against the wall, forming figures like the shadows of women in a chapel-like atmosphere.
Taken Saturday, September 15, 2001, 07:17:45pm.  Original image size: 1200x1600, 427kb
Technical details: Olympus C700UZ, 1/25s @ F3.2, ISO 200, 51mm

Mares library

Mares library

This time we went in to the Mares museum.  In the entrance courtyard, there was some kind of convention of collectors of cards, coins, champagne bottle tops, and who knows what.  Inside most of the museum was more of the same -- it's no coincidence that the collectors chose this location for their get-together -- but this library held many examples of Mares' own sculptures.

##-----------------TITLE------------------------##
Tucker Group
##------------------TEXT------------------------##
Prev: Skocjanske Jame, IIIUp: MiscellaneousNext: Tech Museum Water Park
Tucker Group

A mathematical sculpture by DeWitt Godfrey, unveiled at the Technical Museum of Slovenia as part of the Bled'07 excursion. It depicts a regular map of quadrilaterals, hexagons, and 16-gons on the double torus, the Cayley graph of the unique genus-two group as discovered by Thomas Tucker.
